=500  \\$aFerdinand was the son of Guillaume Staes, organist at the Brussels royal chapel. From 1758, Ferdinand Staes had lessons from his father and later from Ignaz Vitzthumb. He worked as harpsichordist at the Théâtre de la Monnaie in Brussels. In 1767, he was appointed assistant to his father (second organist at the royal chapel). In 1772, Ferdinand Staes became organist at the Madeleine church in Brussels.
=500  \\$aBound in with Staes’ ‘Trois sonates pour le Clavecin ou forte Piano avec accompagnement d'un violon obligé et violoncelle op. 5’, ‘Trois sonates Pour le Clavecin ou forte Piano avec accompagnement d'un violon et violoncelle op. 3’, ‘Concerto pour le clavecin ou le forte piano avec accompagnement de deux violons, alto, viol. contre basse deux flûtes et deux cors op. 6’ and Boccherini’s ‘Six sonates en trio pour le clavecin ou piano forte avec accompagnement de violon et basse - second livre’

=590  \\$aWorinnen die wahre Melodien, derer so wohl in denen beeden Marggrafthümern Bayreuth und Onoltzbach, als auch in der Stadt Nürnberg, deren Gebiete und andern Evangelischen Gemeinen üblichen Kirchen-Lieder, mit aufmerksamster Geflissenheit und Sorgfalt zusammen getragen, und mit einem Signirten Baß versehen zufinden, beedes zum Gebrauch bey dem öffentlichen Gottesdienst auf Orgeln, auch zu Haus zur Ermunterung der Andacht, nebst einem Anhang und historischen Vorrede, von Ursprung, Alterthum, und sondern Merkwürdigkeiten des Chorals

=500  \\$aA blind 18th century musician based in London, Starling Goodwin wrote music both for church use and public concerts. Surviving examples of his work include voluntaries for organ or harpsichord and a number of popular light entertainment songs. One of the greatest pluralists of his profession, he was organist at four London churches simultaneously at the time of his death. He was also a witty and amusing socialiser and an accomplished violinist.

=041  \\$adut$alat

=059  \\$av
=245  \\$aMissen en gezangen
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aUtrecht$bWeyde, van der$c1745
=300  \\$a[i]-48-[2] pages
=336  \\$anotated music
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe so-called 'Stukjesboek', which formed the basis of the old Catholic church song in the Netherlands: 98 songs in Latin and Dutch, plus three ordinaria in Latin. Strong Jansenist influence.
=500  \\$aMissen en Gezangen is not the only para-liturgical hymnbook that the Utrecht Church had after the schism of 1723.
Some of the material it contains had already been published in Het Paradijs, which appeared in eight editions between 1621 and 1679 in Antwerp, or in Het Prieel, Brugues 1609/l0. Also the collection of Gulielmus de Swaen, parish priest in Gouda, to which he gave the name Den Singende Swaen'[, -an allusion to his own name, which means 'swan', - contains pieces that can be found in Missen en Gezangen. Of a substantial part, however, the origin remains obscure. No doubt a large repertoire of Latin and Dutch hymns was known from the rather isolated milieu of the Utrecht church. It is even possible that the type of hymns found in Missen en Gezangen and the other collections mentioned, were cherished by the secular clergy and that their use was discouraged, more or less, by the regulars. It is at least curious that in the Old Catholic Church an abundance of hymns have survived, while they are relatively rare in the Roman Catholic Church parishes in Friesland and northern Holland.
=500  \\$aIn Missen en Gezangen we find texts by Andreas van der Schuur and Jean Baptiste Stalpaert van der Wielen , but most of the texts are from the Counter-Reformation period and are anonymous.
=500  \\$aAndreas van der Schuur (also Van der Schuer) (1656- 1719) was ordained a priest in 1680 and became parish priest in Vianen in 1692. Archbishop Van Neercassel entrusted him with the translation of the Bible  in 1732, completed by H. van Rhijn. He was the composer of several religious poems, both Latin and Dutch.


=500  \\$aJean Baptiste Stalpa(e)rt van der Wiele(n) (1579 - 1630), a lawyer in The Hague in 1598,  became a priest in 1606. In 1613 he was appointed parish priest in Delft, where he remained until his death. In 1621 he published "Hemelrijk", in 1622 "Het vrouwelick cieraed van St Agnes", religious poetry. In prose he published "Roomsche Reys" in 1624, and in 1628 a collection of hymns "'t
Gulden Jaer ons'Heeren Jesu Christi". As a posthumous work he published "Extractum Catholicum" and "Guide Jaers Feestdaghen of de Schat der gheestelijekeLofsanghen", in 1631 and 1634. He was the composer of about 2000 hymns.

=100  \\$aBach, Johann Christian$d1735-1782$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q106641$914631
=240  \\$aOp. 1
=245  \\$aSix Concertos Pour le Clavecin ou Harpe, deux violons, et un violoncelle$bOeuvre 1
=260  \\$aParis$bLe Duc
=300  \\$a33 pages
=500  \\$aKeyboard part only.
=500  \\$aJ C Bach’s set of six harpsichord concertos, Opus 1, was published in March 1763 and dedicated to the eighteen-year-old Queen Charlotte, to whom Bach had recently started giving singing lessons. Princess Charlotte Sophie of Mecklenburg-Strelitz had married King George III on 8 September 1761. She was a passionate music lover, and must have valued the opportunity to have lessons in her own language with a musician of Bach’s calibre. Several of her children were also to receive tuition from Bach, including the future kings George IV and William IV, and Queen Charlotte remained a life-long supporter, even arranging for the return journey of Bach’s wife to her native Italy after his death in 1782.

=563  \\$aEdges of all pages have been restored. New binding in 18th c. style.

=100  \\$aHandel, George Frideric$d1685-1759$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7302$94765
=245  \\$aThe Music in the Alchymist [HWV 43]
=260  \\$aLondon$bArnold$c1787-97
=300  \\$a8 pages
=490  \\$aThe Works of G. F. Händel, Ed. in Score$vplate no. 64
=500  \\$aThe Alchemist, HWV 43, is incidental music used for the revival of Ben Jonson's play The Alchemist at the Queen's Theatre, London on 14 January 1710. The work is an arrangement, by an anonymous composer, of music written by George Frideric Handel.
All but one of the movements were taken from the extended overture to Handel's first Italian opera Rodrigo. The overture introduced the play and the other movements were used to fill the gaps between acts.
The incidental music was published in full a few months after the first performance; however, it is unlikely that Handel received any payment for either the performance or publication of the music. It is likely that the work was the first of Handel's music to be performed in England. 
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Lessons for the Harpsichord First Published in the Year 1720', 'A Second Set of Lessons for the Harpsichord, ‘ A Third Set of Lessons for the Harpsichord’ and ‘Six Fugues or Voluntarys for the Organ or Harpsichord’

=110  \\$4edt$aAllgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (Switzerland)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2648827$921129
=245  \\$aMusicalische Neu-Jahrs-Gedichte von der Music-Gesellschaft auf der Teutschen Schul in Zürich
=260  \\$aZürich$bDeutsche Schule$c1714-40
=300  \\$a224 pages$bmusic, illustrations
=500  \\$aIn the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.
=500  \\$aSee 04J20, 04J21, 10B20, 11H13, G1-027 and G1-028 for similar collections
=500  \\$aEach year between 1713 and 1740 has a New Year's poem and a song with an engraved frontispiece (‘Kupfer-Blatt') bound in, numbered I-XXVIII, but paginated continuously
=500  \\$aThe poems and plates deal predominantly with music, e.g. Jubal's invention of music
=500  \\$aMost songs have Cantus I and Bassus on left page, Cantus II and Altus on right page, but some are for two sopranos only, whose parts face each other; still others have a basso continuo (bassus generalis) part for 'organum'

=260  \\$aPérigueux; Couze; Bordeaux; Bergerac$c1795-1829
=300  \\$a75 pages
=500  \\$aCorrespondence addressed to Schröder and Schylen, traders in the Chatrons in Bordeaux (and some others),  dated between the year Germinal 3 (march 1795) and 1829. 53 letters signed for the most part by Desmartis and Choiet, traders in Bergerac (2 from Courtois in Perigueux and 1 from Dumare in Couze) The Correspondence concerns the delivery of wine. 51 postmarks from Bergerac and 2 from Perigueux. (info Antiquarian)
=500  \\$aThe Bergerac & Périgord (Courtois & Couze) were wine-growing regions, a subregion of South West France,  which corresponds roughly to the current  Dordogne Department. Bordeaux, hub of the famed wine-growing region, is a port city on the Garonne River in southwestern France.

=100  \\$aHumphries, John S.$dc. 1707-1733$4cmp$98160
=245  \\$aXII Sonatas for Two Violins with a Through Bass for the Harpsichord op.1
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bWalsh$c1728
=300  \\$a20-15-15 pages
=500  \\$aAssessed negatively by John Hawkins in his 'History of the Science and Practice of Music' (1776), vol. 5, p. 366: "in the year 1728 he published by subscription twelve Sonatas for two violins and a bass, of a very original cast, in respect that they are in a style somewhat above that of the common popular airs and country-dance tunes, the delight of the vulgar, and greatly beneath what might be expected from the studies of a person at all acquainted with the graces and elegancies of the Italians in their compositions for instruments. To this it must be attributed that the sonatas of Humphries were the common practice of such small proficients in harmony, as in his time were used to recreate themselves with music at alehouse clubs and places of vulgar resort in the village adjacent to London: Of these there were formerly many, in which six-pence at most was the price of admission."

=500  \\$aA mid 18th- or early-19th-century manuscript containing six six sonatas for two violoncellos, with upper staff notated in alto clef. According to Elinor Frey, who inspected the manuscript in Autumn 2023, it is "not immediately appealing music, perhaps [by] an amateur. ... It’s pretty rare to have two-movement sonatas, they all end with the Rondeau (I would place it as German or French sort of "easy" sonata genre, Abel has some of these).

=500  \\$aSupplement to the annual report of the Katharineum Gymnasium 1911
=500  \\$aThe Katharineum in Lübeck was a gymnasium famous for its curriculum of the trivium (grammar, rhetoric and logic), the quadrivium (arithmetic, geometry, music, and astronomy), as well as the study of literature, poetry, drama, philosophy, history, art, and languages.

=500  \\$a Yearbook of the Katharineum in Lübeck, a gymnasium famous for its curriculum of the trivium (grammar, rhetoric and logic), the quadrivium (arithmetic, geometry, music, and astronomy), as well as the study of literature, poetry, drama, philosophy, history, art, and languages.

=500  \\$aChristian Reuter was a German historian and pedagogue and director of the Katharineum in Lübeck 1904-1915. 
=500  \\$aLecture on the history of the gymnasium in separate volume (26E18p)

=246  \1$aThe fraudulent Twelfth Mass
=260  \\$aBonn$bSimrock$c1821
=300  \\$a302 pages
=500  \\$aPlate nr.1815
=500  \\$aThe so called "twelfth mass" by Mozart was published by Simrock coming from a manuscript owned by Zulehner.   In 1826 the authenticity was called into question on stylistic grounds, and Zulehner was unable to come forward with the autograph. It has lang been believed that the Mass was in fact by Zulehner himself. 
=500  \\$aZulehner, when the Mainz Court Orchestra (Mainzer Hofkapelle) was disbanded during the French occupation (1797-1814) bought its library and subsequently, from 1798, supplied copies to local theaters. In 1799 he opened a music store. His publishing house and print works operated from 1802 to 1811 in Mainz, then was continued into the 1820s by his nephew Georg Zulehner (1780–1856) in nearby Eltville in the Rheingau wine region. The total production was 280 plate numbers. Schott of Mainz acquired the company in the 1820s.

=100  \\$aLange, Johann Heinrich$d1784-1856 $4cmp$98241
=245  \\$aChoralbuch zu dem neuen Bremischen Gesangbuch, betitelt Christliches Gesangbuch zur Befördeung öffentlicher und häuslicher Andacht.
=260  \\$aRinteln$bSteuber$c1821
=300  \\$aiv-92 pages$bleather bound, gilded edges$coblong
=500  \\$aJ.H. Lange was organist, singer (tenor), conductor and composer.
=500  \\$aHe was the son of the teacher and organist at St Stephen's in Bremen Johann Lange ( 1755-1815), had his musical training with Peter Winter in Munich, and returned to Bremen in 1804, initially as his father's assistant, before taking over his father's position as organist at St Stephen's in 1809. Lange played first violin in the orchestra of the Privat-Concerte and performed in concerts (especially at the Sing-Akademie) as a tenor. He was also founding member of the Singschule, the Sing-Akademie (later an honorary member) and, in 1827, of the Liedertafel (temporarily its conductor).

=100  \\$aHaydn, Joseph$d1732-1809$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7349$94783
=245  \\$aA Select Collection of Original Scottish Airs for the Voice$nVol. 3
=246  \1$aFifty Scottish Songs, with Symphonies & Acccompaniments, $bWholly by Haydn, Vol. III
=250  \\$a1st ed. 
=260  \\$aLondon$aEdinburg$bPreston$bThomson$c1802
=300  \\$a[i]-4-[ii]-100 pages$balternating pages of text and music, Vol. 3 and Vol. 4 bound together, contains a full page portrait of Robert Burns
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 6 vols., 1793-1841
=500  \\$a"A Select Collection of Original Scottish Airs for the Voice" is a multi-volume collection of Scottish song edited and published by the entrepreneurial musician, publisher and Clerk to the Board of Trustees for Encouragement of Art and Manufacture in Scotland, George Thomson. For the first volume, which appeared in 1793, Thomson commissioned the composer Ignaz Pleyel to provide musical settings.[wikipedia]

From the Preface of this Vol. 3: "For the composition of these [the symphonies and accompaniments], he entered into terms with Mr Pleyel, who fulfilled part of his engagement very satisfactorily; but having then deserted it, the Editor, after a fruitless correspondence with him, which retarded the progress of the Work for years, at length found it necessary to turn his eyes elsewhere. He was so fortunate, however, [...] as to engage Mr Kozeluch and Dr Haydn, to proceed with the Work, which they have finished in such a manner, as to leave him without any other regret, but that of having so long delayed his application to them." 
=500  \\$aContains a portrait of Robert Burns (bound between Vol. 3 and 4) by A. Nasmyth and Paton Thomson. 
=500  \\$aContains a full page engraved illustration "The Soldier's Return", which seems to belong to a song from Vol. 1.
=501  \\$aBound in with Vol. 4 of the same collection.
=590  \\$aWith Introductory & Concluding Symphonies & Accompaniments for the Piano Forte, Violin & Violoncello by Pleyel, Kozeluch & Haydn. With Select & Characteristic Verses both Scottish and English adapted to the Airs, including upwards of One Hundred New Songs by Burns.

=500  \\$aModeled after the French 'Almanach des Muses' (see 09A29, 11A07 and 1B19), the 'Musen-Almanach' was founded in Göttingen in 1770. Johann Heinrich Voß (1751-1826) became its editor in 1774, but in 1775 founded his own almanac in Hamburg (see 06K11-14, H2-134, X3D13).  In 1778 Bürger became editor of the Musenalmanach, a position he retained until his death. Another competing almanac was founded by Schiller (see H3-011 & X1B18)

=245  \\$aDer Kinderfreund.$nEin Wochenblatt$pvolumes 1-12

=300  \\$a12 volumes in 6 (vi-264+viii-268+viii-256+viii-256+xxxiv-256+viii-256+xxxiv-256+xiv-248+viii-264+viii-251+viii-254+viii-261+vi-284 pages)$bplates, illustrations, music examples
=500  \\$a'Der Kinderfreund' was the first children's magazine in Germany. Its editor, Christian Felix Weiße (1726-1804); is considered the German pioneer of juvenile literature.
=500  \\$aBoth H1-036_01 and H1-036_02a-b include volume 3
=500  \\$aVol. 7 has a hand-colored title-page 
=505  \\$gvol. 1 contains the one-act plays 'Der Geburtstag, ein kleines Lustspiel für Kinder' and 'Das Weihnachtsgeschenke', descriptions of an elephant, and Johann Adam Hiller's song 'Freuden des Winters Kinder Lied' -- vol. 2 contains, among others, the plays 'Die Geschwisterliebe' and 'Die Milchschwestern', and Hiller's songs 'Bewohnerin der stillen Hecke' and 'Itzt schulg sie zum letztenmal' -- vol. 3 contains the plays 'Die Schadenfreude, ein kleines Lustspiel für Kinder mit Liederchen' and 'Der ungezogene Knabe', and Hiller's songs 'Ich fahr in tiefe Schachten ein' and 'Armes, kleines, liebes Thier'-- vol. 5 contains the plays 'Wer dem andern eine Grube gräbt, fällt oft selbst hinein oder Die blinde Ruh' and 'Die Schlittenfahrt', and the song 'Ein Kinderlied auf die Geburth des Erlösers' (Welch ein Jubelton!) --  vol. 3 contains Hiller's song ' and the plays 'Die Schadenfreude' and 'Der ungezogene Knabe' -- vol. 4 contains a list of subscribers, the plays 'Edelmuth in Niedrigkeit' and 'Die kleine Aehrenleserinn' -- vol. 6 contains the plays 'Der Abschied' and 'Ein kleiner Familienzwist' -- vol. 7 contains the plays 'Die Ueberraschung' and 'Versprechen muß man halten, oder Ein guter Mensch macht andre gute Menschen' - vol. 8 contains the plays 'Die Friedensfeyer, oder Die unvermuthete Wiederkunst' and 'Die natürliche Zauberey' --  vol. 9 contains songs by Hiller and the plays 'Das junge Modefrauenzimmer' and 'Gute Kinder der Aeltern größter Reichthum' -- vol. 10 contains the plays 'Ein gutes Herz macht manchen Fehler gut' and 'Die Freunde, oder Das Vogelschießen' --  vol. 11 contains the plays 'Die Feuersbrunst, oder Gute Freunde in der Noth das größte Glück' and 'Das Windspiel, oder Die Rache' -- vol. 12 contains the plays 'Die jungen Spieler, oder Böse Gesellschaften verderben gute Sitten' and 'Das Denkmal in Arkadien'

=500  \\$aAmbrosius Lobwasser was a German humanist and translator, born in Saxony. He is best known for this Psalter des Königlichen Propheten David , published in 1573 (Leipzig). This metrical psalter, a translation of the French Genevan psalter by Clément Marot and Théodore de Bèze, became one of the standard psalm-books used by the evangelical churches of the German-speaking lands, including Switzerland. The Lobwasser psalter was widely reprinted into the 1800s.

=100  \\$aHagedorn, Friedrich von$d1708-1754$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q63985$96793
=245  \\$aDes herrn Friedrichs von Hagedorn sämmtliche poetische Werke$nvols. 1-3
=260  \\$aHamburg$bBohn$c1771
=300  \\$a3 vols. in 1 (xxviii-130-[2]+178-[10]+xxii-180-[2] pages)$bfrontispiece engraving, engraved title page
=500  \\$aHagedorn incorporated ancient, French and above all English inspirations into cheerful, sensible fables and tales (1738) and anacreontic, dallying odes and songs (1742-1752). Formally, his works can be divided into fables, songs, didactic poems and epigrams. His poetry is kept simple (alternating verse, easily singable stanzaic forms) and pursues different stylistic ideals than the poets of the Baroque. 
=500  \\$aMozart set his poem Die Alte (The Old Woman) in his song of the same name (K. 517) in 1787. Joseph Haydn set two of his poems in his canons (a capella songs) (Hob. XXVIIb).

=500  \\$aOlof Åhlström (1756-1835) was an organist and composer. His own compositions include a large number of songs, among them many poems by Anna Maria Lenngren, who was his sister-in-law, that he had set to music. These were published in several parts of Skalde-stycken satte i musik (1794–1823). He also composed a number of chorales, a cantata, fourteen sonatas, and an opera, Frigga (1787).

=100  \\$aLa Marre, De$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q41796210$97981
=245  \\$aLes Chansons pour danser et pour boire
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bBallard$c1650
=300  \\$a[iv]-43-[3] pages$bengraved title-page
=500  \\$aGuillo 2003 n° 1650-D; RISM L 350
=500  \\$aLa Marre, whose first name is unknown, was active as a French composer, instrumentalist and dancer in the second third of the 17th century. He is known to have contributed to, among others, the 'Ballet royal de la nuit' (1653), 'Les noces de Thétis et Pélée' (1654), 'Le Ballet d'Alcidiane' (1658), 'Hercule amoureux' (1662), and 'Le Ballet des Muses' (1666).
=500  \\$aDedicated to Henri Prévost, "maître à danser du roi", dancing master of the french king Louis XIV until 1652.
Prévost was amongst the most prominent dancing masters in the kingdom, and one of the 13 first  « académistes » who in 1661 established Académie royale de danse.

=501  \\$aBound in with 'IV. livre des chansons du Sieur de Chancy, maistre de la musique de la Chambre du Roy', 'XVI. livre des chansons pour danser et pour boire', 'XVII. livre des chansons pour danser et pour boire', 'Les Chansons pour danser et pour boire Du Sieur Guyot', and 'V. livre des chansons du Sieur de Chancy, maistre de la musique de la chambre du Roy'

=501  \\$aBound in with 'Les Chansons pour danser et pour boire Du Sieur De La Marre', 'XVI. livre des chansons pour danser et pour boire', 'XVII. livre des chansons pour danser et pour boire', 'Les Chansons pour danser et pour boire Du Sieur Guyot', and 'V. livre des chansons du Sieur de Chancy, maistre de la musique de la chambre du Roy'

=520  \\$aFrançois de Chancy (1600–1656) was a French singer, lutenist, and composer. He was a master of music for Cardinal Richelieu in 1631, master of chamber music (1635) and was chamber musician of the Chapelle royale (1649). François de Chancy was highly regarded by Mersenne, who included Chancy's pieces in his treatises.

=100  \\$aPinot Duclos, Charles$d1704-1772$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q982034$98370
=245  \\$aHistoire de Madame De Luz;  anecdotte du règne d'Henri IV
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bHondt, de$c1741
=300  \\$a426-22 pages$btitle page in red and black ink
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThrough a vivid portrait of a woman of sovereign innocence, Duclos denounces the hypocrisy of a prudish society. Madame de Luz is a sort of libertine Princess of Cleves, a moralist's novel that is also a praise of femininity.
=504  \\$aMadame de Luz is one of the most beautiful women in the kingdom of Henry IV, virtuous and loyal to her husband. She is secretly in love with the Marquis de Saint-Geran, but tries to forget this passion.

Her husband, the Baron de Luz, is involved in a plot led by the Maréchal de Biron, Governor of Burgundy, to overthrow Henry IV. Arrested, the Baron de Luz is threatened with the death penalty. Convinced of his innocence and determined to free him, Madame de Luz intervenes with one of the judges at the trial, Monsieur de Thurin, a suitor whom she had once spurned. Thurin is ready to clear the Baron's name if she accepts his advances. Madame de Luz resists and then gives in to the blackmail. Her life then turns upside down. She has committed a sin from which she will never recover.

=500  \\$aFirst edition of this curious and unusual work, in which the author, physician to the polish King Stanislas (Stanisław I Leszczyński 1677-1766) seeks to study the "influence of the passions" on the development of diseases: this is one of the first treatises on the subject, which was very popular at the end of the 18th and beginning of the 19th centuries. =245  \\$aFour Private Libraries of New York: A Contribution to the History of Bibliophilism in America

=300  \\$a119 pages$bunpaginated pages with illustrations (engravings, photos, litographs), title page in red and black ink, coloured and black&white llithographs preceded by a tissue, front and back matter consists of each 10 blanco pages
=500  \\$aHenri Pène du Bois, an American writer, literary critic, and journalist whose friendship with French author Guy de Maupassant (1850-1893) was the source of his son’s name. Born in a cultured, sophisticated family of French origin but with roots in America dating back to 1748, he was an avowed francophile and created a sophisticated environment deeply engaged in the French culture. He accompanied his son Guy, a painter, on a trip to Paris in 1905. His tragic death in 1906 on board of the ship for their return home to America forced Guy to turn to art criticism to help support his family.

=500  \\$aDes Maizeaux translated the works of Charles de Saint-Évremond in English from the French published in 1714 during his exile in England. The book also described the author's life, a translation from his "La Vie de St Evremond", published in 1711.
=500  \\$aCharles de Marguetel de Saint-Denis, seigneur de Saint-Évremond, was a French soldier, hedonist, essayist and literary critic. After 1661, he lived in exile, mainly in England, as a consequence of his attack on French policy. He wrote for his friends and did not intend his work to be published, although a few of his pieces were leaked in his lifetime. The first full collection of his works was published in London in 1705, after his death.

=500  \\$a"Mr L'Abbé de Villiers, si connu par son Art de prêcher, & par plusieurs autres Ouvrages, qui ont eu l'aprobation du public" (in Oeuvres de Monsieur de Saint Evremond, I,  p.296)
=500  \\$aDe Villiers wrote many works in the seventeenth century, and many biographies and studies are attributed to him, such as Lettres sur l'oraison des quiétistes or Prière en vers sur l'espérance qu'on doit avoir en Jésus-Christ.He  was the first to suspect that Perrault's tales were not written by Charles Perrault's son, as announced by the publishers, but by the academician himself - or at least at second hand. De Villiers joined the Jesuits on 6 June 1666 and distinguished himself in the careers of teaching and preaching. He took the order of priesthood and exercised the holy ministry. In 1689 he left the Jesuits to join the unreformed Cluny order. A writer and essayist, he composed or printed most of the works that came from his pen. Boileau mentions the Abbé de Villiers in his poetry, and calls him "the Matamore of Cluny", "because he had a bold air and imperious speech". He never put his name to his works.

=500  \\$aHenriette-Julie de Murat was an aristocratic French writer of the late 17th century.
=500  \\$aIn 1697 she published Memoirs of the Countess of M***, a two-volume collection of false "memoirs" which was meant as a response to Charles de Saint-Évremond's 1696 book Memoirs of the Life of Count D*** before his Retirement, which had portrayed women as incapable of virtue and fickle. Murat's book was successful and was even translated into English.

=500  \\$aLe Misant(h)rope was a Dutch journal originally published every monday from May 19th 1711 tot December 26th 1712 . Published in 2 vols. in The Hague by T.Johnson in 1711 and 1712. The magazine was reprinted in 1726 (own revision by Van Effen) in The Hague; 1741 (Lausanne/Geneva) and twice in 1742 (Amsterdam and The Hague).
=500  \\$aJustus van Effen was a Dutch author, who wrote chiefly in French but also made crucial contributions to Dutch literature. A journalist, he imitated The Spectator with the publication of the Dutch-language Hollandsche Spectator. He gained international fame as a writer of French periodicals and a translator from English into French, and he is also recognized as one of the most important Dutch language writers of the 18th century and an influential figure of the Dutch Enlightenment
=500  \\$aOften considered as one of the best essayistic texts from the early Enlightenment.
=500  \\$aFrontispiece vol.1 is an engraved portrait of the author by Pieter Tanjé (1706-1761)  after des Angeles (1716-1761)

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aEffen, Justus van$d1684-1735$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2574405$98518
=245  \\$aLa Bagatelle, $bou Discours ironiques$n1-2/2
=250  \\$arev. ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bUytwerf$c1742
=300  \\$a2 vols ([xxvi]-300-[8] + 289-[9] pages)$btitle pages in red and black ink
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=490  \\$aOeuvres diverses de Mr. Juste van Effen$v3-4/4
=500  \\$aMoral observations in a satirical tone. Interests: fashion, religion, morals. Authors studied: Addison, Swift, La Bruyère.
=500  \\$aDutch Journal published every thursday and monday between 5 mai 1718 and 13 avril 1719. 
=500  \\$aAlready the author of several journals including the first spectator in French (Le Misanthrope), Justus van Effen attempted to capture the Regency spirit in France with La Bagatelle. Produced as a twice-weekly quarter sheet, La Bagatelle included witty observations on contemporary society, literary controversies, bolder, more subversive reflections on questions of religion, as well as short works of poetry and prose. 
=500  \\$aSince 1718, the publication of the Literary Journal had been delayed by the nonchalance of the bookseller Johnson. For van Effen this meant a considerable loss of money, so he sought some compensation. He launched La Bagatelle for personal reasons.
=500  \\$aThe author intended (cf. Preface) to lead men from the ridiculousness of custom and fashion to Reason; but his ironic style was not understood. Convinced of his error, he wanted to change his plan: "I will put a capital I on the frontispiece of my Feuille Volante, so that the public will be aware of it" (I, as in Irony), he declares at the end of the first volume. In fact, van Effen himself, a serious man, found it difficult to sustain the satirical tone. In short, La Bagatelle was not a success.
=500  \\$aPreface in the issue of Monday 5 September 1718: "to bring Men back from the ridiculous impressions of Custom and Fashion to the eternal and invariable principles of Reason, which must be the only Rule of our Conduct".
=504  \\$aevery volume contains an index
=504  \\$aEdited by James L. Schorr (ed.), ‘La Bagatelle’ (1718-1719): a critical edition of Justus van Effen’s journal, in  'Oxford University Studies in the Enlightenment', November 2014. ISBN 9780729411493, 352 pages,
=590  \\$aOù l'on prête des Sophismes ingénieux au Vice & à l'Extravagance, pour en faire mieux sentir le ridicule. Par Mr. van Effen, Docteur en Droit, & Membre de la Société Royale de Londres

=100  \\$aDrouaux, Étienne$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q28494512$98519
=245  \\$aMéthode nouvelle pour apprendre le plain-chant$bDivise en quatre parties

=300  \\$a[viii]-144 pages$bmusical examples
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1672 Paris by Robert & Ballard
=500  \\$aÉtienne Drouaux was a musician and composer active in Paris in the last third of the 17th century.
=500  \\$aDrouaux is best known as the author of a method of plainsong which enjoyed a certain success, since about ten editions were published between 1672 and 1705. This method was part of a wave of publications of new methods which tended to give a somewhat secure basis to the practice of plainchant. But it appears that Drouaux was largely inspired by Jean Millet's method of 1666, keeping the most practical elements and eliminating the old authorities that encumbered it.
=500  \\$aDrouaux' first name is really Étienne (or Estienne), not Henri Blaise, as Fétis or Ton thought

=100  \\$aMaffei, Scipione$d1675-1755$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1587432$96886
=245  \\$aDe gli anfiteatri e singolarmente del Veronese $blibri due
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aVerona$bTumermani$c1728
=300  \\$a[12]-348-[12] pages, 14 inserted folded pages with plates$bbound in white vellum, illustrations, engraved title page
=500  \\$aMaffei was a Venetian writer and art critic, author of many articles and plays. An antiquarian with a humanist education whose publications on Etruscan antiquities stand as incunables of Etruscology. Founder of the Lapidary Museum of Verona. A multifaceted figure in the Italian and European panorama. Military, philosopher, poet, playwright, historian, scientist, opera librettist, but above all a passionate fanatic of antiquities. He was an avid collector of ancient manuscripts and epigraphs, which he acquired in Verona, Italy or brought from all over the Mediterranean basin thanks to the possessions of the Republic of Venice, of which Verona was a part. Maffei was a prominent member of the Veronese Accademia Filarmonica and he worked for the realization of the theater that would be inaugurated in 1732 with Vivaldi's 'La fida ninfa', for which he wrote the libretto.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aMaggi, Girolamo$dc. 1523-1572$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q5564769$98540
=245  \\$aDe equuleo
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bFrisius$c1664
=300  \\$a[xxx]-196-[14] pages$bbound in white vellum, engraved title page, illustrations, 1 inserted folded page$c7x13 cm
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aTreatise on torture devices written in 1571, first published posthumously 1609.
=500  \\$aMaggi was an Italian scholar, jurist, poet, military engineer, urban planner, philologist, archaeologist, mathematician, and naturalist who studied at Bologna under Francis Robortello. He authored several works, including a collection of poems on the Flemish wars, and several on the subject of philosophy.
=500  \\$aMaggi was a judge and military defense engineer in Famagusta on Cyprus when the island was invaded by Ottoman Turks in 1571. Besieged by the Turks, he invented machines to defend Famagusta against their attacks. When the island was conquered, Maggi was sent to the dungeons at Constantinople where, locked in chains, he wrote from memory two detailed treatises, De tintinnabulis, on bells and carillons, and the explicitly illustrated De equuleo, on torture devices.In attempts to be freed, he dedicated the first treatise to Carolus Rym (Charles Ramire), ambassador to the Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian II, and the second treatise to François de Noailles, bishop of Aire and ambassador to the King of France. They were pleased with his works, and endeavoured to obtain his release. Their efforts, however, were brought to light as he was being released to the Italian ambassador. The prison captain ordered him to be detained and executed by strangulation. His two treatises were published posthumously in 1608 and 1609, respectively.

=041  \\$ager$hdan
=100  \\$aHolberg, Ludvig$d1684-1754$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q216692$98546
=245  \\$aPeter Paars$bein comisches Heldengedicht
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bMumme$c1750
=300  \\$a[lxviii]-420 pages$b14 inserted engraved plates, engraved title pages and frontispiece
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aTitle page has emblem "In Spe et Labore"
=500  \\$aPeder Paars is a comic-epic poem that appeared in four parts in the years 1719-20 under the pseudonym of Hans Michelsen. The poem is a parody of the heroic epics of antiquity and Renaissance. Holberg particularly alludes to Vergil's great Roman epic Aeneid.
=500  \\$aThe poem enjoyed great success, but the description of conditions on Anholt prompted the then owner, Frederik Rostgaard, to complain to the king, demanding that the book be burned by the executioner. The king nevertheless decided that the writing - although it "could rather have been omitted than written" - could be accepted, as it was a "fictitious sketch." 
=500  \\$aHolberg was a writer, essayist, philosopher, historian and playwright born in Bergen, Norway, during the time of the Dano-Norwegian dual monarchy. He was influenced by Humanism, the Enlightenment and the Baroque. Holberg is considered the founder of modern Danish and Norwegian literature. He is best known for the comedies he wrote in 1722–1723 for the Lille Grønnegade Theatre in Copenhagen.
=500  \\$aPaars was a breakthrough in Holberg's writing in the direction of satire and the many comedies for which he is still known.
=500  \\$aThe composer J.A. Scheibe translated Peder Paars into German. In 1740 he became kapellmeister at the court of the danisch king Christian IV, and remained in Denmark until his death. He had a very sharp pen, evident in his satirical writings or political pamphlets,  but also in the first biography of his friend Baron Ludvig Holberg, The biography not only provides information on Holberg but also indirectly on Scheibe.
=504  \\$aPaars and his crew discover that the inhabitants of Anholt, who "live Christianly and feed on debris", are plundering and robbing the castaways. The rest of the island is watching the commoners who live in the blackest superstition. The bailiff passes judgement in his own favour, while the priest relies on old Catholic sermons.

https://www.hf.uio.no/imv/english/research/projects/power/projectdescription/holberg/

=520  \\$aLady Truman is apparently widowed when she receives word that her husband Sir George has been killed in battle during the recent war. As she is now the wealthy owner of an estate she is pursued by two suitors, but concerningly the house is disturbed at night by repeated sounds of ghostly drumming. After the drumming has scared off the two suitors Mr. Tinsel and Mr. Fantome it is revealed to be the work of Sir George, still very much alive.

=500  \\$aJohann Joseph Kausch was a Silesian physician and writer. He not only wrote various writings and treatises in the field of medicine, but also published writings on aesthetics, poetry and politics. In Trachenberg, as personal physician at the court of Prince Franz Philipp Adrian Hatzfeld (1717-1779), he began to study psychology through the study of French philosophers.

=024  \\$2Wikidata$aQ3320970
=041  \\$alat$hlat
=245  \\$aMonita secreta of de geheime instructiën die door de Jesuieten in stilte worden nageleefd
=260  \\$aOostburg$bBronswijk$c1868
=300  \\$a56 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAnti-Jesuit pamphlet
=500  \\$aThe Monita secreta ("Secret Instructions") is an anonymous document from 1614 whose original title is Monita privata Societatis Iesu . This booklet gives instructions to the Jesuits on how to proceed in order to gain power and wealth. It is a fake - and known as such since 1615 - but it had great success with the enemies of the Jesuits, including the 19th and 20th centuries.  Scholars regard the document as an anti-Jesuit forgery, written by Hieronymus Zahorowski, a Jesuit dismissed from the Order.
=520  \\$aAccording to the Monita, Jesuits are to use every means at their disposal to acquire wealth for the order. For instance, Jesuits are encouraged to entice promising young men to enter the order and endow it with their estates; rich widows are to be cajoled and dissuaded from remarriage. Every means is to be used for the advancement of Jesuits to bishoprics or other ecclesiastical dignities and to discredit the members of other orders, while the world is to be persuaded that the Society is animated by the purest and least interested motives: the reputation of those who quit it is to be assailed and maligned in every way.

=245  \\$aLes Psaumes de David, mis en vers françois, & les cantiques sacrés
=250  \\$aRev. ed.
=260  \\$aBasel$bImhof$c1774
=300  \\$a472-180 pages$bgilded edges
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aIncluding one loose page with ms. notes about psalmbooks, probably written by D.W.L. Milo, on the backside of a concert flyer.
=500  \\$aThe translation of the psalms go back to John Calvin (1509-1564). In 1562 a collection of psalms (known as the Genevan Psalms) was published, suitable to be sung during the service. Calvin had started rhyming in Strasbourg himself. Back in Geneva, he handed this work over to Clément Marot and Beza, while he asked Guillaume Franc, Louis Bourgeois and Maitre Pierre to compose the music. Calvin's zeal in making a collection of psalms arose from his wish to use the Bible alone, also for the hymn. Later editions were edited by members of the 'Compagnie des pasteurs de l'église protestante de Genève'. 
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1698

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aDorat, Claude-Joseph$d1734-1780$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q361456$98577
=245  \\$aLes Prôneurs, ou Le Tartuffe littéraire,$bComédie en trois actes, en vers.
=260  \\$aParis$bDelalain$c1777
=300  \\$aviii-87 pages$b4 insterted engravings
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aA lively satire of the people in Julie de Lespinasse's society, i.e. the philosophical party. Dorat kept it in his portfolio for several years without being able to have it performed. The philosophers, who were not spared, used the powerful men of their party to prevent the play from being performed. The main character of the play is D'Alembert who, under the name of "Callidès", plays the role of leader of the advocates. The scene in which he initiates a young follower into the mysteries of the order is very pleasant. In this play we find some portraits drawn with a rather vigorous brush, among others, those of Palissot and Clément de Dijon, of whom Dorat had reason to complain; of the former, because he had portrayed him in a less than advantageous manner in his Dunciade; of the latter, because he had made a bitter criticism of his poem De la déclamation.
=500  \\$amotto by Voltaire on the frontispiece: "Le Philosophe est seul, & l'Imposteur fait Secte."
=500  \\$aDorat published most of his works with numerous engravings by Clément-Pierre Marillier and Charles Eisen, which made them masterpieces of art and typographic luxury
=500  \\$a4 beautiful engravings after Clément-Pierre Marillier (1740-1808), by Pierre Duffos le Jeune (1742-1816) , Louis Michel Halbou (1730-1809) and Pierre Adrien Le Beau (1744-1804)

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aDe Nederlandsche Spectator $nvolumes 1-12
=260  \\$aLeiden$bvan der Eyk$c1749-60
=300  \\$a12 vols ([v]-216+[iv]-208+ [iv]-216+[iv]-216+[iv]-208+[iv]-224+[iv]-218+[iv]-208+[iv]-208+[iv]-224+[iv]-208+[iv]-208-[58] pages)$bengraved title page, one folded page with notated music in volume 8
=500  \\$a12 identical engraved title-vignettes by Jan Wandelaar (1690-1759): Theseus and Ariadne walk through a landscape. Ariadne holds a thread from the globe yarn in Theseus' hands. The show is largely surrounded by a spell band on which the words Virtutis Amore and the reference to the eighth book of Ovidius' metamorphoses, in which the story is.
=500  \\$aComplete set of this fortnightly Spectator, of which a total of 312 issues were published, each of eight pages. In the first issue, the unknown editor gives a profile of some of his friends who will assist him: they know their languages, each of them has a special expertise, some love poetry, and all, the editor included, are Protestant, "this is enough as far as they and I are concerned." The name of one of his collaborators has become well known: the Alkmaar rector and Neo-Latin poet E.W. Higt (1723 - 1762). 
=500  \\$aThere is a table of contents in the front of each volume and volume XII contains an index to all volumes. 
=500  \\$aThe title was used twice more towards the end of the eighteenth century: in 1786 for an Amsterdam weekly, but publisher J. Verlem (or editor H. Bergh) changed the name to 'De Nederlandsche spectator met de bril' already after 14 issues, and in 1792 for an Utrecht periodical, edited by H. van Otterloo, of which 50 issues appeared.
=500  \\$aThe Nederlandsche Spectotor was following the example of the english 'The Spectator', a periodical published since 1711 by Joseph Addison and Sir Richard Steele, both politicians, and one of the bestsellers of the 18th century. Its 500 issues sold up to 4000 copies a day, and carried news and comment, but especially comments on manners, morals and literature. The publication pretended to be the reports by a Mr Spectator on the conversations of a club comprising representatives of the country squirearchy, the town, commerce and the army.

=100  \\$aVolkmann, Johann Jacob$d1732-1803$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q113563$98583
=245  \\$aHistorisch-kritische Nachrichten von Italien $p1-3/3
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bFritsch$c1770-1
=300  \\$a3 vols. (xxvi-682-[8] + viii-872 + [viii]-846-[42] pages)$bengraved frontispiece, red edges, engraved title vignet
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOne of the most influential German art books of the 18th century. Spread over three volumes, it systematically provides information about churches, palaces, art collections, musical life, but also about the history of all important Italian cities from Turin to Naples. As a guide to historical Italy, the 'Volkmann' accompanied Goethe, Karl Philipp Moritz, Johann Gottfried Seume and many other Germans on their travels. Goethe, for example, wrote to Charlotte von Stein in 1787: " I am now reading the good, dry Volckmanns zweyten Theil to note what I have not yet seen." (Kippenberg)
=500  \\$a3 identical engraved title vignets depicting 2 little boys holding a map of Italy
=500  \\$aFrontispiece engraving by Christian Gottlieb Geyser (1742-1803)
=500  \\$amanuscript notes on front matter of vol. 1 and 2
=500  \\$apensil markings throughout
=561  \\$aEx libris Riegel- und Wiesnersche Lesebibliothek Nürnberg (plate)
=590  \\$awelche eine Beschreibung dieses Landes, der Sitten und Gebraüche, der Regierungsform, Handlung, Oekonomie, des Zustandes der Wissenschaften und insonderheit der Werke der Kunst nebst einer Beurtheilung derselben enthalten. Aus den neuesten französischen und englischen Reisebeschreibungen und aus eignen Anmerkungen zusammengetragen.

=500  \\$aJohan Georg Hamann was a German librettist and writer, a cousin of his famous nephew of the same name J. G. Hamann (1730-1788). He became a private tutor and was active as a publicist, contributing to Gottsched's periodical 'Die vernünftigen Tadlerinnen'. 
=500  \\$aHe wrote for Georg Philipp Telemann: the libretto to the opera 'Margaretha, Queen of Castile' (Hamburg 1730), translated Metastasio's recitatives of  Didone abbandonata for 'Der Streit der kindlichen Pflicht, oder, Die Flucht des Aeneas nach Latien' (Hamburg 1731), and the libretto for the opera 'Der Weiseste in Sidon' (Hamburg 1733).
=590  \\$aNebst einer kurtzen Erklärung der mythologischen Nahmen, aus den besten und neuesten deutschen Dichtern zusammen getragen, und der studirenden Jugend zum bequemen Gebrauch an statt eines Poetischen Lexici, mit einer Anweisung zur reinen und wahren Deutschen Dicht-Kunst ans Licht gestellet.

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aadress book of Berlin in 1764
=500  \\$aThe Berlin address calendars appeared annually between 1704 and 1918 under different titles.
=500  \\$aThe Berlin address calendars list the higher-ranking persons and office holders of the royal Prussian residential cities of Berlin and Potsdam as well as their authorities, administrations and organizations. The address and description of the authorities are listed, as well as the person's name, official title and private address. At the end of each entry is an index of names. From 1878 onwards, information from the neighboring city of Charlottenburg is also included.

=245  \\$aAmusemens philologiques en prose et en vers$bou mélange agréable de diverses pièces, concernant l'histoire des personnes célèbres, les évènemens mémorables & l'histoire naturelle$p3

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aLater edition
=500  \\$aoriginal in 2 vols. , 1749-1750
=500  \\$aChoffin was a scholar and philologist, born in Héricourt (F) on October 2, 1703, died in Halle (D) in January 1773.  He obtained the double position of professor of modern languages at the school of the Orphans and at the university of Halle, and he contributed by his writings and his lessons to spread the use of French in Saxony.
=500  \\$aEditor's emblem depicting sunbeams & cultivated land with saying "illo splendete levabor' and the initials WH, referring to Weisenhaus Halle  (La Maison des Orphelins à Halle). The Latin motto "Illo splendente levabor" (By his splendor I will be exalted) was intended to testify to the godliness of the institution. The sower in the foreground was interpreted by Bible-loving contemporaries as a reference to the Gospel of Mark (4:14): "The sower sows the word." And this was precisely Francke's basic concern: to change the world by means of the word.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aGodeau, Antoine$d1605-1672$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q586272$97907
=245  \\$aPoësies chrestiennes
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bPetit$c1660
=300  \\$a508 pages$bengraved title page
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAntoine Godeau was a French bishop, poet and exegete.
=500  \\$aAntoine Godeau (1605-1672) first published the Poësies Chrestiennes in 1633 in the context of the Catholic Reformation which encouraged spiritual revival. This lyric collection is emblematic of his comprehensive poetic and spiritual work. Godeau became the Bishop of Grasse in 1636 and devoted his poetic gifts to enlightening the readers. This new edition is the latest version of the Poësies Chrestiennes (1660), which is pastoral Catholic verse addressed to the socialites of the time. The versatile poet expressed himself in various forms, registers and topics to convey the Christian dogma and the Bible. The content and the purpose of the book fluctuated. The Poësies chrestiennes was thus a field for experimentation : it became Antoine Godeau's laboratory for all his pastoral and lyric work. The poet defined the principles of a poetry which was based on the conciliation of divine enthusiasm and reason, a poetry where grace and beauty met. The paraphrase of the Scriptures was an opportunity to explore the conciliation of Parnassus and Calvary, as well as the specificity of a classical poetic language in the making, endowing it with gentleness and clarity. Poetry appeared to be the ideal way to instill Christian truths in the heart of the faithful. The religious conversion of secular literary rhetoric prepared the layman to hear the poet-preacher’s vigorous speech. Antoine Godeau tempered his Augustinian anthropology by promoting a life both wordly and pious, in chime with the ideal of Christian “honnêteté”. The poet spiritualized profane aesthetics, which showed his unrelenting desire to adapt his conversion discourse to a public eager to be edified by the “delectare”.
=504  \\$aCamille Venner, Édition critique des "Poësies chrestiennes" (1660) d'Antoine Godeau précédée d'une introduction sur la pastorale lyrique et catholique de cet auteur, These, Université de Lorraine, 2018
https://hal.univ-lorraine.fr/tel-01752385

=100  \\$aSaavedra Fajardo, Diego de$d1584-1648$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2715411$98592
=245  \\$aIdea de un principe politico christiano, representada en cien empresas

=300  \\$a[xxxv]-983 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aDiego de Saavedra Fajardo (1584-1648) was a Spanish diplomat and man of letters.

=500  \\$ain 1640 Saavedra published the anti-Machiavellian emblem book Empresas Políticas. Idea de un príncipe político cristiano, a hundred short essays about the education of a prince. This work was written primarily for the son of King Philip IV. It passed through a number of editions and was translated in several languages.
=500  \\$aSaavedra's 'Idea de un príncipe político cristiano' was a very erudite work that uses the literary sort of emblem, put by Andrea Alciato with his 'Emblemata' translated in 1549 and that has a mainly moral and philosophical character. His work, however, was mainly inspired by the 'Emblemata política' (1618), by Jakob Bruck Angermunt, being the intention of the author to compose a guide for the suitable political formation of a Christian prince. 
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1640

=041  \\$alat$afre
=245  \\$aCantus diversi pro Dominicis, festis et feriis per annum
=260  \\$aToulouse$bDouladoure$c1745
=300  \\$a286 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$apages 282-286 include a 'Manière pour bien chanter dans un chœur' (without title page), derived from 'Trois methodes faciles pour apprendre le plein-chant' (1689).
=500  \\$aThis set of three anonymous methods could have been commissioned by Claude Bachelu, a bookseller from Lyon who was worried on several occasions for counterfeiting or for having distributed banned books. Having published numerous works of spirituality and theology, Bachelu brought out in his name a collection of Cantus diversi (1689). Like Parisian colleagues such as La Caille, he doubled this publication with a theoretical counterpart, thus the 'Trois methodes'. Modeled from the easy method designed for the Parisian seminary of Saint-Nicolas du Chardonnet, they then benefited from a long editorial existence since they are found at the end of several other books imitating that of Bachelu, and this until the middle of the 18th century. The 'Three methods' are (partly) included with a new title page and new compositions in the Cantus diversi by Claude Moulu (Lyon, 1700) and by Gaspard Henault (Toulouse, 1745) or, without title page, in the Cantus diversi ex Graduali Romano by Pierre Valfray (Lyon, 1724) and this edition by Joseph Douladure (Toulouse, 1745). (for more information see: https://www.cantus-scholarum.univ-tours.fr/ressources/sources/methodes-faciles-de-plain-chant/trois-methodes-1698/)
=500  \\$ams. scribblings on back matter

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aMoritz von Strachwitz (1822-1847) was a German lyric poet. When traveling in Italy in 1847 he was taken ill in Venice, and died in Vienna. Although he had thus only reached his twenty-fifth year, he revealed a lyric genius of remarkable force and originality. His early death was a great loss to German letters; for he was by far the most promising of the younger lyric poets of his time.

=260  \\$aParis$bGuerin$bDelatour$c1761
=300  \\$axii-164 pages$b2 fold-out plates
=500  \\$aFirst electric-powered musical instrument ever, invented in 1759 by Delaborde (also De Laborde, De La Borde, Thillais, Thillaès, 1730-1777). Delaborde exposes his invention in "deux Lettres adressées aux Auteurs des Mémoires de Trévoux" (p. iii), i.e. the Jesuit journal that had been edited by Louis Bertrand Castel, inventor of the 'clavecin oculaire' (to which Delaborde refers). The first letter is dated 15 June 1759, the other 3 August 1759.

=245  \\$aNouveaux mémoires ou observations sur l'Italie et sur les Italiens, par deux gentilshommes suédois$n1-3/3
=260  \\$aLondon$bNourse$c1764
=300  \\$a3 vols. ([iv]-396 + [ii]-488 + 412 pages)$bTitle page in red and black ink, leather bound, gold embossed spine, red edges
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aFollowing his sojourn in Italy in 1745 and 1746, as the military administrator of the maréchal de Maillebois during the War of Austrian Succession, Grosley published his 'Observations sur l'Italie et les Italiens' using his proper name as author. 
For his 'New Memoires or Observations on Italy' of 1764 he used the anonymous "two Swedish gentlemen" as pseudonym, and introduced them as fictional characters who would have made the journey through italy.
=500  \\$aEx Libris Mme de Chauvelin et Mr d'Imécourt :  The Countess de Mérode sold the land of Louppy by a contract dated 1st May 1741 to François Théodore de Custine de Wiltz. Married, but without posterity, he designated his nephew Marie Louis Charles de Vassinhac d'Imécourt as his heir, who married in 1778 Charlotte Ferdinande de Chauvelin, lady-in-waiting of Madame Elisabeth of France, daughter of the Marquis de Chauvelin, lieutenant general, Grand Cross of Saint Louis, ambassador to Turin, master of the Guard Robe of King Louis XV.
